   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Visual impairment
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
     <span class="mw-redirectedfrom">
      (Redirected from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/w/index.php?title=Blindness&amp;redirect=no" title="Blindness">

      )
     </span>
    </div>

         </a>

          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>

       <tr class="noprint">
        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
         <div style="text-align: right;">
          [
          <a class="extiw" href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q737460" title="d:Q737460">
           edit on Wikidata
          </a>
          ]
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <b>
        Visual impairment
       </b>
       , also known as
       <b>
        vision impairment
       </b>
       or
       <b>
        vision loss
       </b>
       , is a decreased ability to
       <a href="/wiki/Visual_perception" title="Visual perception">
        see
       </a>
       to a degree that causes problems not fixable by usual means, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Glasses" title="Glasses">
        glasses
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHODef_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-WHODef-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC2011_2-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-CDC2011-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some also include those who have a decreased ability to see because they do not have access to glasses or
       <a href="/wiki/Contact_lens" title="Contact lens">
        contact lenses
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHODef_1-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-WHODef-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Visual impairment is often defined as a best corrected
       <a href="/wiki/Visual_acuity" title="Visual acuity">
        visual acuity
       </a>
       of worse than either 20/40 or 20/60.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mab2006_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mab2006-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The term
       <b>
        blindness
       </b>
       is used for complete or nearly complete vision loss.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mab2006_5-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mab2006-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Visual impairment may cause people difficulties with normal daily activities such as driving, reading, socializing, and walking.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC2011_2-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-CDC2011-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The most common causes of visual impairment globally are uncorrected
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Refractive_errors" title="Refractive errors">
        refractive errors
       </a>
       (43%),
       <a href="/wiki/Cataract" title="Cataract">
        cataracts
       </a>
       (33%), and
       <a href="/wiki/Glaucoma" title="Glaucoma">
        glaucoma
       </a>
       (2%).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2014_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-WHO2014-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Refractive errors include
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Near_sighted" title="Near sighted">
        near sighted
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Far_sighted" title="Far sighted">
        far sighted
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Presbyopia" title="Presbyopia">
        presbyopia
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astigmatism_(eye)" title="Astigmatism (eye)">
        astigmatism
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2014_3-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-WHO2014-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cataracts are the most common cause of blindness.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2014_3-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-WHO2014-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other disorders that may cause visual problems include
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Age_related_macular_degeneration" title="Age related macular degeneration">
        age related macular degeneration
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Diabetic_retinopathy" title="Diabetic retinopathy">
        diabetic retinopathy
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corneal_opacification" title="Corneal opacification">
        corneal clouding
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Childhood_blindness" title="Childhood blindness">
        childhood blindness
       </a>
       , and a number of
       <a href="/wiki/Infection" title="Infection">
        infections
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2012Data_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-WHO2012Data-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Visual impairment can also be caused by problems in the
       <a href="/wiki/Brain" title="Brain">
        brain
       </a>
       due to
       <a href="/wiki/Stroke" title="Stroke">
        stroke
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Premature_birth" title="Premature birth">
        premature birth
       </a>
       , or trauma among others.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leh2012_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Leh2012-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These cases are known as
       <a href="/wiki/Cortical_visual_impairment" title="Cortical visual impairment">
        cortical visual impairment
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leh2012_7-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Leh2012-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Screening for vision problems in children may improve future vision and educational achievement.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Screening adults without symptoms is of uncertain benefit.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USPSTF2016_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-USPSTF2016-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Diagnosis is by an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eye_exam" title="Eye exam">
        eye exam
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC2011_2-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-CDC2011-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">
        World Health Organization
       </a>
       (WHO) estimates that 80% of visual impairment is either preventable or curable with treatment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2014_3-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-WHO2014-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This includes cataracts, the infections
       <a href="/wiki/Onchocerciasis" title="Onchocerciasis">
        river blindness
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Trachoma" title="Trachoma">
        trachoma
       </a>
       , glaucoma, diabetic retinopathy, uncorrected refractive errors, and some cases of childhood blindness.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2015Cause_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-WHO2015Cause-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many people with significant visual impairment benefit from
       <a href="/wiki/Vision_rehabilitation" title="Vision rehabilitation">
        vision rehabilitation
       </a>
       , changes in their environment, and assistive devices.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC2011_2-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-CDC2011-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As of 2015 there were 940 million people with some degree of vision loss.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GBD2015Pre_4-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-GBD2015Pre-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       246 million had low vision and 39 million were blind.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2014_3-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-WHO2014-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The majority of people with poor vision are in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_world" title="Developing world">
        developing world
       </a>
       and are over the age of 50 years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2014_3-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-WHO2014-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Rates of visual impairment have decreased since the 1990s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2014_3-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-WHO2014-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Visual impairments have considerable economic costs both directly due to the cost of treatment and indirectly due to decreased ability to work.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">
        Classification
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Visual_impairment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Classification">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Snellen_chart.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1624" data-file-width="1303" height="324" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Snellen_chart.svg/260px-Snellen_chart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Snellen_chart.svg/390px-Snellen_chart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Snellen_chart.svg/520px-Snellen_chart.svg.png 2x" width="260"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Snellen_chart.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A typical
         <a href="/wiki/Snellen_chart" title="Snellen chart">
          Snellen chart
         </a>
         that is frequently used for
         <a href="/wiki/Visual_acuity" title="Visual acuity">
          visual acuity
         </a>
         testing.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The definition of visual impairment is reduced vision not corrected by
       <a href="/wiki/Glasses" title="Glasses">
        glasses
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Contact_lens" title="Contact lens">
        contact lenses
       </a>
       . The World Health Organization uses the following classifications of visual impairment. When the vision in the better eye with best possible glasses correction is:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        20/30 to 20/60 : is considered mild vision loss, or near-normal vision
       </li>
       <li>
        20/70 to 20/160 : is considered moderate visual impairment, or moderate low vision
       </li>
       <li>
        20/200 to 20/400 : is considered severe visual impairment, or severe low vision
       </li>
       <li>
        20/500 to 20/1,000 : is considered profound visual impairment, or profound low vision
       </li>
       <li>
        More than 20/1,000 : is considered near-total visual impairment, or near total blindness
       </li>
       <li>
        No light perception : is considered total visual impairment, or total blindness
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Blindness is defined by the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">
        World Health Organization
       </a>
       as vision in a person's best eye with best correction of less than 20/500 or a
       <a href="/wiki/Visual_field" title="Visual field">
        visual field
       </a>
       of less than 10 degrees.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mab2006_5-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mab2006-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This definition was set in 1972, and there is ongoing discussion as to whether it should be altered to officially include uncorrected refractive errors.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHODef_1-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-WHODef-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">
        United Kingdom
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Visual_impairment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Severely sight impaired
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Defined as having central visual acuity of less than 3/60 with normal fields of vision, or gross visual field restriction.
       </li>
       <li>
        Unable to see at 3 metres what the normally sighted person sees at 60 m.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Sight impaired
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Able to see at 3 m, but not at 6 m, what the normally sighted person sees at 60 m
       </li>
       <li>
        Less severe visual impairment is not captured by registration data, and its prevalence is difficult to quantify
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Low vision
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        A visual acuity of less than 6/18 but greater than 3/60.
       </li>
       <li>
        Not eligible to drive and may have difficulty recognising faces across a street, watching television, or choosing clean, unstained, co-ordinated clothing.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
         <a href="#cite_note-12">
          [12]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       In the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK" title="UK">
        UK
       </a>
       , the Certificate of Vision Impairment (CVI) is used to certify patients as severely sight impaired or sight impaired.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The accompanying guidance for clinical staff states: "The National Assistance Act 1948 states that a person can be certified as severely sight impaired if they are "so blind as to be unable to perform any work for which eye sight is essential". The test is whether a person cannot do any work for which eyesight is essential, not just his or her normal job or one particular job."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dh.gov.uk_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-dh.gov.uk-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In practice, the definition depends on individuals'
       <a href="/wiki/Visual_acuity" title="Visual acuity">
        visual acuity
       </a>
       and the extent to which their
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Field_of_vision" title="Field of vision">
        field of vision
       </a>
       is restricted. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Department_of_Health" title="Department of Health">
        Department of Health
       </a>
       identifies three groups of people who may be classified as severely visually impaired.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dh.gov.uk_14-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-dh.gov.uk-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        Those below 3/60 (equivalent to 20/400 in US notation)
        <a href="/wiki/Snellen_chart" title="Snellen chart">
         Snellen
        </a>
        (most people below 3/60 are severely sight impaired).
       </li>
       <li>
        Those better than 3/60 but below 6/60 Snellen (people who have a very contracted field of vision only).
       </li>
       <li>
        Those 6/60 Snellen or above (people in this group who have a contracted
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Field_of_vision" title="Field of vision">
         field of vision
        </a>
        especially if the contraction is in the lower part of the field).
       </li>
      </ol>
      <p>
       The Department of Health also state that a person is more likely to be classified as severely visually impaired if their eyesight has failed recently or if they are an older individual, both groups being perceived as less able to adapt to their vision loss.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dh.gov.uk_14-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-dh.gov.uk-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">
        United States
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Visual_impairment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: United States">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In the United States, any person with vision that cannot be corrected to better than 20/200 in the best eye, or who has 20 degrees (diameter) or less of visual field remaining, is considered
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legally_blind" title="Legally blind">
         legally blind
        </a>
       </i>
       or eligible for disability classification and possible inclusion in certain government sponsored programs.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the United States, the terms
       <i>
        partially sighted
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        low vision
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        legally blind
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        totally blind
       </i>
       are used by schools, colleges, and other educational institutions to describe students with visual impairments.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They are defined as follows:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <i>
         Partially sighted
        </i>
        indicates some type of visual problem, with a need of person to receive special education in some cases.
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         Low vision
        </i>
        generally refers to a severe visual impairment, not necessarily limited to distance vision. Low vision applies to all individuals with sight who are unable to read the newspaper at a normal viewing distance, even with the aid of eyeglasses or contact lenses. They use a combination of vision and other senses to learn, although they may require adaptations in lighting or the size of print, and, sometimes,
        <a href="/wiki/Braille" title="Braille">
         Braille
        </a>
        .
        <ul>
         <li>
          <i>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Myopia" title="Myopia">
            Myopic
           </a>
          </i>
          – unable to see distant objects clearly, commonly called near-sighted or short-sighted.
         </li>
         <li>
          <i>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyperopia" title="Hyperopia">
            Hyperopic
           </a>
          </i>
          – unable to see close objects clearly, commonly called far-sighted or long-sighted.
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         Legally blind
        </i>
        indicates that a person has less than 20/200 vision in the better eye after best correction (contact lenses or glasses), or a field of vision of less than 20 degrees in the better eye.
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         Totally blind
        </i>
        students learn via Braille or other non-visual media.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       In 1934, the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Medical_Association" title="American Medical Association">
        American Medical Association
       </a>
       adopted the following definition of blindness:
      </p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>
        Central visual acuity of 20/200 or less in the better eye with corrective glasses or central visual acuity of more than 20/200 if there is a visual field defect in which the peripheral field is contracted to such an extent that the widest diameter of the visual field subtends an angular distance no greater than 20 degrees in the better eye.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Koestler_16-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Koestler-16">
          [16]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </p>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">
        United States Congress
       </a>
       included this definition as part of the Aid to the Blind program in the
       <a href="/wiki/Social_Security_(United_States)#Creation:_The_Social_Security_Act" title="Social Security (United States)">
        Social Security Act
       </a>
       passed in 1935.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Koestler_16-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Koestler-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corn_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Corn-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1972, the Aid to the Blind program and two others combined under Title XVI of the Social Security Act to form the
       <a href="/wiki/Supplemental_Security_Income" title="Supplemental Security Income">
        Supplemental Security Income
       </a>
       program
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which states:
      </p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>
        An individual shall be considered to be blind for purposes of this title if he has central visual acuity of 20/200 or less in the better eye with the use of a correcting lens. An eye which is accompanied by a limitation in the fields of vision such that the widest diameter of the visual field subtends an angle no greater than 20 degrees shall be considered for purposes of the first sentence of this subsection as having a central visual acuity of 20/200 or less. An individual shall also be considered to be blind for purposes of this title if he is blind as defined under a State plan approved under title X or XVI as in effect for October 1972 and received aid under such plan (on the basis of blindness) for December 1973, so long as he is continuously blind as so defined.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
         <a href="#cite_note-19">
          [19]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </p>
      </blockquote>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other">
        Other
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Visual_impairment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Other">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">
        Kuwait
       </a>
       is one of many nations that share the 6/60 criteria for legal blindness.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Al-Merjan_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Al-Merjan-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Health_effects">
        Health effects
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Visual_impairment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Health effects">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Visual impairments may take many forms and be of varying degrees. Visual acuity alone is not always a good predictor of the degree of problems a person may have. Someone with relatively good acuity (e.g., 20/40) can have difficulty with daily functioning, while someone with worse acuity (e.g., 20/200) may function reasonably well if their visual demands are not great.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/American_Medical_Association" title="American Medical Association">
        American Medical Association
       </a>
       has estimated that the loss of one eye equals 25% impairment of the visual system and 24% impairment of the whole person;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-colenbrander_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-colenbrander-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       total loss of vision in both eyes is considered to be 100% visual impairment and 85% impairment of the whole person.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-colenbrander_21-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-colenbrander-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Some people who fall into this category can use their considerable residual vision – their remaining sight – to complete daily tasks without relying on alternative methods. The role of a low vision specialist (optometrist or ophthalmologist) is to maximize the functional level of a patient's vision by optical or non-optical means. Primarily, this is by use of magnification in the form of telescopic systems for distance vision and optical or electronic magnification for near tasks.
      </p>
      <p>
       People with significantly reduced acuity may benefit from training conducted by individuals trained in the provision of technical aids. Low
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vision_Rehabilitation" title="Vision Rehabilitation">
        vision rehabilitation
       </a>
       professionals, some of whom are connected to an agency for the blind, can provide advice on lighting and contrast to maximize remaining vision. These professionals also have access to non-visual aids, and can instruct patients in their uses.
      </p>
      <p>
       The subjects making the most use of rehabilitation instruments, who lived alone, and preserved their own mobility and occupation were the least depressed, with the lowest risk of suicide and the highest level of social integration.
      </p>
      <p>
       Those with worsening sight and the prognosis of eventual blindness are at comparatively high risk of suicide and thus may be in need of supportive services. These observations advocate the establishment and extension of therapeutic and preventative programs to include patients with impending and current severe visual impairment who do not qualify for services for the blind. Ophthalmologists should be made aware of these potential consequences and incorporate a place for mental health professionals in their treatment of these types of patients, with a view to preventing the onset of depressive symptomatology, avoiding self-destructive behavior, and improving the quality of life of these patients. Such intervention should occur in the early stages of diagnosis, particularly as many studies have demonstrated how rapid acceptance of the serious visual handicap has led to a better, more productive compliance with rehabilitation programs. Moreover, psychological distress has been reported (and is exemplified by our psychological autopsy study) to be at its highest when sight loss is not complete, but the prognosis is unfavorable.10 Therefore, early intervention is imperative for enabling successful psychological adjustment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Associated_problems">
        Associated problems
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Visual_impairment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Associated problems">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Blindness can occur in combination with such conditions as
       <a href="/wiki/Intellectual_disability" title="Intellectual disability">
        intellectual disability
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autism_spectrum_disorders" title="Autism spectrum disorders">
        autism spectrum disorders
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cerebral_palsy" title="Cerebral palsy">
        cerebral palsy
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hearing_impairment" title="Hearing impairment">
        hearing impairments
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Epilepsy" title="Epilepsy">
        epilepsy
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lighthouse_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-lighthouse-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autism_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-autism-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Blindness in combination with hearing loss is known as
       <a href="/wiki/Deafblindness" title="Deafblindness">
        deafblindness
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       It has been estimated that over half of completely blind people have
       <a href="/wiki/Non-24-hour_sleep%E2%80%93wake_disorder" title="Non-24-hour sleep–wake disorder">
        non-24-hour sleep–wake disorder
       </a>
       , a condition in which a person's
       <a href="/wiki/Circadian_rhythm" title="Circadian rhythm">
        circadian rhythm
       </a>
       , normally slightly longer than 24 hours, is not
       <a href="/wiki/Entrainment_(chronobiology)" title="Entrainment (chronobiology)">
        entrained
       </a>
       (synchronized) to the light/dark cycle.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AASM2008_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AASM2008-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cause">
        Cause
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Visual_impairment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Cause">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The most common causes of visual impairment globally in 2010 were:
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Refractive_error" title="Refractive error">
         Refractive error
        </a>
        (42%)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Cataract" title="Cataract">
         cataract
        </a>
        (33%)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Glaucoma" title="Glaucoma">
         glaucoma
        </a>
        (2%)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Age_related_macular_degeneration" title="Age related macular degeneration">
         age related macular degeneration
        </a>
        (1%)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corneal_opacification" title="Corneal opacification">
         corneal opacification
        </a>
        (1%)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Diabetic_retinopathy" title="Diabetic retinopathy">
         diabetic retinopathy
        </a>
        (1%)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Childhood_blindness" title="Childhood blindness">
         childhood blindness
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Trachoma" title="Trachoma">
         trachoma
        </a>
        (1%)
       </li>
       <li>
        undetermined (18%)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2012Data_6-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-WHO2012Data-6">
          [6]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ol>
      <p>
       The most common causes of blindness in 2010 were:
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        cataracts (51%)
       </li>
       <li>
        glaucoma (8%)
       </li>
       <li>
        age related macular degeneration (5%)
       </li>
       <li>
        corneal opacification (4%)
       </li>
       <li>
        childhood blindness (4%)
       </li>
       <li>
        refractive errors (3%)
       </li>
       <li>
        trachoma (3%)
       </li>
       <li>
        diabetic retinopathy (1%)
       </li>
       <li>
        undetermined (21%)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2012Data_6-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-WHO2012Data-6">
          [6]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ol>
      <p>
       About 90% of people who are visually impaired live in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_world" title="Developing world">
        developing world
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2014_3-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-WHO2014-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Age-related macular degeneration, glaucoma, and diabetic retinopathy are the leading causes of blindness in the developed world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bunce_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bunce-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Among working age adults who are newly blind in England and Wales the most common causes in 2010 were:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        Hereditary retinal disorders (20.2%)
       </li>
       <li>
        Diabetic retinopathy (14.4%)
       </li>
       <li>
        Optic atrophy (14.1%)
       </li>
       <li>
        Glaucoma (5.9%)
       </li>
       <li>
        Congenital abnormalities (5.1%)
       </li>
       <li>
        Disorders of the visual cortex (4.1%)
       </li>
       <li>
        Cerebrovascular disease (3.2%)
       </li>
       <li>
        Degeneration of the macula and posterior pole (3.0%)
       </li>
       <li>
        Myopia (2.8%)
       </li>
       <li>
        Corneal disorders (2.6%)
       </li>
       <li>
        Malignant neoplasms of the brain and nervous system (1.5%)
       </li>
       <li>
        Retinal detachment (1.4%)
       </li>
      </ol>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cataracts">
        Cataracts
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Visual_impairment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Cataracts">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Of these, cataract is responsible for &gt;65%, or more than 22 million cases of blindness, and glaucoma is responsible for 6 million cases.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cataracts" title="Cataracts">
        Cataracts
       </a>
       : is the congenital and pediatric pathology that describes the greying or opacity of the crystalline lens, which is most commonly caused by intrauterine infections, metabolic disorders, and genetically transmitted syndromes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Althomali,_T._2012_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Althomali,_T._2012-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cataracts are the leading cause of child and adult blindness that doubles in prevalence with every ten years after the age of 40.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brian,_G._2001_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brian,_G._2001-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Consequently, today cataracts are more common among adults than in children.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Althomali,_T._2012_30-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Althomali,_T._2012-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       That is, people face higher chances of developing cataracts as they age. Nonetheless, cataracts tend to have a greater financial and emotional toll upon children as they must undergo expensive diagnosis, long term rehabilitation, and visual assistance.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Also, according to the Saudi Journal for Health Sciences, sometimes patients experience irreversible amblyopia
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Althomali,_T._2012_30-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Althomali,_T._2012-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       after pediatric cataract surgery because the cataracts prevented the normal maturation of vision prior to operation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Despite the great progress in treatment, cataracts remain a global problem in both economically developed and developing countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At present, with the variant outcomes as well as the unequal access to cataract surgery, the best way to reduce the risk of developing cataracts is to avoid smoking and extensive exposure to sun light (i.e. UV-B rays).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brian,_G._2001_31-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brian,_G._2001-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Glaucoma">
        Glaucoma
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Visual_impairment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Glaucoma">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Glaucoma" title="Glaucoma">
        Glaucoma
       </a>
       is a congenital and pediatric eye disease characterized by increased pressure within the eye or intraocular pressure (IOP).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-go.galegroup.com_35-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-go.galegroup.com-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Glaucoma causes visual field loss as well as severs the optic nerve.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-glaucoma.org_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-glaucoma.org-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Early diagnosis and treatment of glaucoma in patients is imperative because glaucoma is triggered by non-specific levels of IOP.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-glaucoma.org_36-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-glaucoma.org-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Also, another challenge in accurately diagnosing glaucoma is that the disease has four causes: 1) inflammatory ocular hypertension syndrome (IOHS); 2) severe uveitic angle closure; 3) corticosteroid-induced; and 4) a heterogonous mechanism associated with structural change and chronic inflammation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-go.galegroup.com_35-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-go.galegroup.com-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In addition, often
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pediatric_glaucoma" title="Pediatric glaucoma">
        pediatric glaucoma
       </a>
       differs greatly in cause and management from the glaucoma developed by adults.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Meszaros,_Liz_2013_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Meszaros,_Liz_2013-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Currently, the best sign of pediatric glaucoma is an IOP of 21 mm Hg or greater present within a child.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Meszaros,_Liz_2013_37-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Meszaros,_Liz_2013-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       One of the most common causes of pediatric glaucoma is cataract removal surgery, which leads to an incidence rate of about 12.2% among infants and 58.7% among 10-year-olds.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Meszaros,_Liz_2013_37-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Meszaros,_Liz_2013-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Infections">
        Infections
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Visual_impairment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Infections">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:68-4062-1_(ATED).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="679" data-file-width="913" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/68-4062-1_%28ATED%29.jpg/220px-68-4062-1_%28ATED%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/68-4062-1_%28ATED%29.jpg/330px-68-4062-1_%28ATED%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/68-4062-1_%28ATED%29.jpg/440px-68-4062-1_%28ATED%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:68-4062-1_(ATED).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The burden of
         <a href="/wiki/Onchocerciasis" title="Onchocerciasis">
          onchocerciasis
         </a>
         : children leading blind adults in Africa
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Childhood blindness can be caused by conditions related to pregnancy, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Congenital_rubella_syndrome" title="Congenital rubella syndrome">
        congenital rubella syndrome
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Retinopathy_of_prematurity" title="Retinopathy of prematurity">
        retinopathy of prematurity
       </a>
       . Leprosy and onchocerciasis each blind approximately 1 million individuals in the developing world.
      </p>
      <p>
       The number of individuals blind from
       <a href="/wiki/Trachoma" title="Trachoma">
        trachoma
       </a>
       has decreased in the past 10 years from 6 million to 1.3 million, putting it in seventh place on the list of causes of blindness worldwide.
      </p>
      <p>
       Central corneal ulceration is also a significant cause of monocular blindness worldwide, accounting for an estimated 850,000 cases of corneal blindness every year in the Indian subcontinent alone. As a result, corneal scarring from all causes is now the fourth greatest cause of global blindness.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Injuries">
        Injuries
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Visual_impairment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Injuries">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Re-educating_wounded._Blind_French_soldiers_learning_to_make_baskets._American_Red_Cross.,_1917_-_1919_-_NARA_-_533674.tif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2266" data-file-width="3000" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Re-educating_wounded._Blind_French_soldiers_learning_to_make_baskets._American_Red_Cross.%2C_1917_-_1919_-_NARA_-_533674.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Re-educating_wounded._Blind_French_soldiers_learning_to_make_baskets._American_Red_Cross.%2C_1917_-_1919_-_NARA_-_533674.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Re-educating_wounded._Blind_French_soldiers_learning_to_make_baskets._American_Red_Cross.%2C_1917_-_1919_-_NARA_-_533674.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Re-educating_wounded._Blind_French_soldiers_learning_to_make_baskets._American_Red_Cross.%2C_1917_-_1919_-_NARA_-_533674.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Re-educating_wounded._Blind_French_soldiers_learning_to_make_baskets._American_Red_Cross.%2C_1917_-_1919_-_NARA_-_533674.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Re-educating_wounded._Blind_French_soldiers_learning_to_make_baskets._American_Red_Cross.%2C_1917_-_1919_-_NARA_-_533674.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Re-educating_wounded._Blind_French_soldiers_learning_to_make_baskets._American_Red_Cross.,_1917_-_1919_-_NARA_-_533674.tif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Re-educating wounded. Blind French soldiers learning to make baskets, World War I.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Eye injuries, most often occurring in people under 30, are the leading cause of monocular blindness (vision loss in one eye) throughout the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       . Injuries and cataracts affect the eye itself, while abnormalities such as
       <a href="/wiki/Optic_nerve_hypoplasia" title="Optic nerve hypoplasia">
        optic nerve hypoplasia
       </a>
       affect the nerve bundle that sends signals from the eye to the back of the brain, which can lead to decreased visual acuity.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Cortical_blindness" title="Cortical blindness">
        Cortical blindness
       </a>
       results from injuries to the
       <a href="/wiki/Occipital_lobe" title="Occipital lobe">
        occipital lobe
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Human_brain" title="Human brain">
        brain
       </a>
       that prevent the brain from correctly receiving or interpreting signals from the
       <a href="/wiki/Optic_nerve" title="Optic nerve">
        optic nerve
       </a>
       . Symptoms of cortical blindness vary greatly across individuals and may be more severe in periods of exhaustion or stress. It is common for people with cortical blindness to have poorer vision later in the day.
      </p>
      <p>
       Blinding has been used as an
       <a href="/wiki/Blinding_(punishment)" title="Blinding (punishment)">
        act of vengeance and torture
       </a>
       in some instances, to deprive a person of a major sense by which they can navigate or interact within the world, act fully independently, and be aware of events surrounding them. An example from the classical realm is
       <a href="/wiki/Oedipus" title="Oedipus">
        Oedipus
       </a>
       , who gouges out his own eyes after realizing that he fulfilled the awful prophecy spoken of him. Having crushed the Bulgarians, the Byzantine Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Basil_II" title="Basil II">
        Basil II
       </a>
       blinded as many as 15,000 prisoners taken in the battle, before releasing them.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Contemporary examples include the addition of methods such as
       <a href="/wiki/Acid_throwing" title="Acid throwing">
        acid throwing
       </a>
       as a form of
       <a href="/wiki/Disfigurement" title="Disfigurement">
        disfigurement
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Genetic_defects">
        Genetic defects
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Visual_impairment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Genetic defects">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       People with
       <a href="/wiki/Albinism" title="Albinism">
        albinism
       </a>
       often have vision loss to the extent that many are legally blind, though few of them actually cannot see.
       <a href="/wiki/Leber%27s_congenital_amaurosis" title="Leber's congenital amaurosis">
        Leber's congenital amaurosis
       </a>
       can cause total blindness or severe sight loss from birth or early childhood.
      </p>
      <p>
       Recent advances in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genetic_map" title="Genetic map">
        mapping
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Human_genome" title="Human genome">
        human genome
       </a>
       have identified other genetic causes of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_vision" title="Low vision">
        low vision
       </a>
       or blindness. One such example is
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bardet-Biedl_syndrome" title="Bardet-Biedl syndrome">
        Bardet-Biedl syndrome
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Poisoning">
        Poisoning
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Visual_impairment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Poisoning">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Rarely, blindness is caused by the intake of certain chemicals. A well-known example is
       <a href="/wiki/Methanol" title="Methanol">
        methanol
       </a>
       , which is only mildly toxic and minimally intoxicating, and breaks down into the substances
       <a href="/wiki/Formaldehyde" title="Formaldehyde">
        formaldehyde
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Formic_acid" title="Formic acid">
        formic acid
       </a>
       which in turn can cause blindness, an array of other health complications, and death.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Methanol_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Methanol-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       When competing with
       <a href="/wiki/Ethanol" title="Ethanol">
        ethanol
       </a>
       for metabolism, ethanol is metabolized first, and the onset of toxicity is delayed. Methanol is commonly found in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Methylated_spirits" title="Methylated spirits">
        methylated spirits
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Denatured_alcohol" title="Denatured alcohol">
        denatured ethyl alcohol
       </a>
       , to avoid paying taxes on selling ethanol intended for human consumption. Methylated spirits are sometimes used by
       <a href="/wiki/Alcoholism" title="Alcoholism">
        alcoholics
       </a>
       as a
       <a href="/wiki/Surrogate_alcohol" title="Surrogate alcohol">
        desperate and cheap substitute
       </a>
       for regular ethanol
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverages" title="Alcoholic beverages">
        alcoholic beverages
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_2">
        Other
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Visual_impairment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Other">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Amblyopia" title="Amblyopia">
         Amblyopia
        </a>
        : is a category of vision loss or visual impairment that is caused by factors unrelated to refractive errors or coexisting ocular diseases.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rashad,_M._A._2012_41-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Rashad,_M._A._2012-41">
          [41]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Amblyopia is the condition when a child's visual systems fail to mature normally because the child either suffers from a premature birth, measles, congenital nubella syndrome, vitamin A deficiency, or meningitis.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gilbert,_C._2001_42-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Gilbert,_C._2001-42">
          [42]
         </a>
        </sup>
        If left untreated during childhood, amblyopia is currently incurable in adulthood because surgical treatment effectiveness changes as a child matures.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gilbert,_C._2001_42-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-Gilbert,_C._2001-42">
          [42]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Consequently, amblyopia is the world's leading cause of child monocular vision loss, which is the damage or loss of vision in one eye.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rashad,_M._A._2012_41-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-Rashad,_M._A._2012-41">
          [41]
         </a>
        </sup>
        In the best case scenario, which is very rare, properly treated amblyopia patients can regain 20/40 acuity.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rashad,_M._A._2012_41-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-Rashad,_M._A._2012-41">
          [41]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corneal_opacification" title="Corneal opacification">
         Corneal opacification
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Myopia#Degenerative_myopia" title="Myopia">
         Degenerative myopia
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Diabetic_retinopathy" title="Diabetic retinopathy">
         Diabetic retinopathy
        </a>
        : is one of the manifestation microvascular complications of diabetes, which is characterized by blindness or reduced acuity. That is, diabetic retinopathy describes the retinal and vitreous hemorrhages or retinal capillary blockage caused by the increase of A1C,
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morello,_C._M_2007_43-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Morello,_C._M_2007-43">
          [43]
         </a>
        </sup>
        which a measurement of blood glucose or sugar level.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
         <a href="#cite_note-44">
          [44]
         </a>
        </sup>
        In fact, as A1C increases, people tend to be at greater risk of developing diabetic retinopathy than developing other microvascular complications associated with diabetes (e.g. chronic hyperglycemia, diabetic neuropathy, and diabetic nephropathy).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morello,_C._M_2007_43-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-Morello,_C._M_2007-43">
          [43]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Despite the fact that only 8% of adults 40 years and older experience vision-threatening diabetic retinopathy (e.g. nonproliferative diabetic retinopathy or NPDR and proliferative diabetic retinopathy or PDR), this eye diseased accounted for 17% of cases of blindness in 2002.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morello,_C._M_2007_43-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-Morello,_C._M_2007-43">
          [43]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Retinitis_pigmentosa" title="Retinitis pigmentosa">
         Retinitis pigmentosa
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Retinopathy_of_prematurity" title="Retinopathy of prematurity">
         Retinopathy of prematurity
        </a>
        : The most common cause of blindness in infants worldwide. In its most severe form, ROP causes retinal detachment, with attendant visual loss. Treatment is aimed mainly at prevention, via laser or
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avastin" title="Avastin">
         Avastin
        </a>
        therapy.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stargardt%27s_disease" title="Stargardt's disease">
         Stargardt's disease
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Uveitis" title="Uveitis">
         Uveitis
        </a>
        : is a group of 30 intraocular inflammatory diseases
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sciencedirect.com_45-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-sciencedirect.com-45">
          [45]
         </a>
        </sup>
        caused by infections, systemic diseases, organ-specific autoimmune processes, cancer or trauma.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rao,_Narsing_2013_46-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Rao,_Narsing_2013-46">
          [46]
         </a>
        </sup>
        That is, uveitis refers to a complex category of ocular diseases that can cause blindness if either left untreated or improperly diagnosed.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rao,_Narsing_2013_46-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-Rao,_Narsing_2013-46">
          [46]
         </a>
        </sup>
        The current challenge of accurately diagnosing uveitis is that often the cause of a specific ocular inflammation is either unknown or multi-layered.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sciencedirect.com_45-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-sciencedirect.com-45">
          [45]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Consequently, about 3–10% uveitis victims in developed countries, and about 25% of victims in the developing countries, become blind from incorrect diagnosis and from ineffectual prescription of drugs, antibiotics or steroids.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rao,_Narsing_2013_46-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-Rao,_Narsing_2013-46">
          [46]
         </a>
        </sup>
        In addition, uveitis is a diverse category of eye diseases that are subdivided as granulomatous (or tumorous) or non-granulomatous anterior, intermediate, posterior or pan uveitis.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rao,_Narsing_2013_46-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-Rao,_Narsing_2013-46">
          [46]
         </a>
        </sup>
        In other words, uveitis diseases tend to be classified by their anatomic location in the eye (e.g. uveal tract, retina, or lens), as well as can create complication that can cause cataracts, glaucoma, retinal damage, age-related macular degeneration or diabetic retinopathy.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rao,_Narsing_2013_46-4">
         <a href="#cite_note-Rao,_Narsing_2013-46">
          [46]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Xerophthalmia" title="Xerophthalmia">
         Xerophthalmia
        </a>
        , often due to
        <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_A_deficiency" title="Vitamin A deficiency">
         vitamin A deficiency
        </a>
        , is estimated to affect 5 million children each year; 500,000 develop active corneal involvement, and half of these go blind.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Diagnosis">
        Diagnosis
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Visual_impairment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Diagnosis">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <div class="PopUpMediaTransform" id="mwe_player_0" style="width:220px;" videopayload='&lt;div class="mediaContainer" style="width:640px"&gt;&lt;video id="mwe_player_1" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Exploring-Eye-Movements-in-Patients-with-Glaucoma-When-Viewing-a-Driving-Scene-pone.0009710.s001.ogv/640px--Exploring-Eye-Movements-in-Patients-with-Glaucoma-When-Viewing-a-Driving-Scene-pone.0009710.s001.ogv.jpg" controls="" preload="none" autoplay="" style="width:640px;height:480px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="49.72" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Exploring-Eye-Movements-in-Patients-with-Glaucoma-When-Viewing-a-Driving-Scene-pone.0009710.s001.ogv" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/b/bc/Exploring-Eye-Movements-in-Patients-with-Glaucoma-When-Viewing-a-Driving-Scene-pone.0009710.s001.ogv/Exploring-Eye-Movements-in-Patients-with-Glaucoma-When-Viewing-a-Driving-Scene-pone.0009710.s001.ogv.480p.webm" type="video/webm;
